===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\help_topics\First_Topic.htm =====

Introduction to GEO GEO is an integrated a PC-based integrated well log authoring, analysis and reporting system which has been developed for petroleum geologists, geoscientists and engineers.
Building upon concepts that the software should be easy to learn, simple and intuitive to use, and invoking our 'you should only have to do it once' method of working, Geologix has developed and enhanced the GEO suite of applications with continuous input from our users.
The GEO applications provide flexible integrated and tailored solutions for managing both well-site and laboratory derived data, by combining a powerful yet extremely compact database, with a user-friendly graphical interface.
You can manipulate curve data, lithology blocks, modifiers, symbols and text with the mouse and keyboard, to log information into the database.
Is it a versatile software that may be used to create an infinite variety of user-defined plot presentations.
Some examples are well proposal charts, lithology logs, composite logs, well summary logs, drilling time charts, gas analysis, quick-look water saturation and pore pressure charts plots.
Content can be fully customized to suit individual or corporate preferences.
Lithology patterns, modifiers, symbols, headers and trailers can all be designed or modified by you to match existing or standard log requirements.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Introduction\Application_Look.htm =====

The refers to the GEO interface style.
If you wish to change this, open the Tools tab and click on - a range of 'Looks' will invoke.
Select as desired and the interface will automatically change.
To return to the classic GEO interface (i. e. non ribbons), on the Tools tab, check Classic View.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Introduction\GEO_License_and_Version_Number.htm =====

Your software level and version are written at the top at the GEO -About box that is invoked.
Apart from these software details, this box also provides the following information: Additional modules, if any ODF (Database ) version Licence name and licence number Type of dongle ( CodeMeter/Flexnet )
Note that it is the security-device (dongle) provided with your software that determines the level of your software (i. e. GEO or GEO Lite ), any supplied additional modules, and thus the accessible features.
The software version however is determined by the software installed from CD-ROM (or web-downloaded update).
You can therefore upgrade the level of your installation easily at any time (e. g. from GEO Lite to GEO ) by simply substituting a new dongle supplied by Geologix Limited.
You don’t need to re-install the application, except when upgrading from GEO Logger.

• Additional modules, if any
• ODF (Database) version
• Licence name and licence number
• Type of dongle (CodeMeter/Flexnet)

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Introduction\RUS_Rental_Dongle_Guide.htm =====

RUS Rental Dongle Guide RUS Rental Dongle Guide The RUS ( Remote Update Service )
Dongle is specially configured to be used for rented licenses of our applications.
This new style of renting gives greater flexibility for rental terms and also increased access to updates.
The clock on your machine now governs your rental periods.
A license will run from one set date and time to another set date and time.
The period between these two dates will be when you can access your GEO Software Suite application.
Should you require more time on the current rental or foresee a period where you may require the GEO Software Suite again, a new license file can be sent via e-mail to update your dongles validity.
The update file that is used to update the validity of your CodeMeter RUS license requires a. WibuCmRaU file.
The update file is used to update the validity of your RUS dongle.
WibuCmRaU file contains the information pertaining to the rental period.
These files can be sent directly via e-mail and can instantly be applied to gain access to GEO Software Suite applications.
Updating a License/License Expiry This can be done in two ways depending on the current status of the license in the RUS dongle.
An extension can also be applied after the license has expired, this is detailed below.
If a rental period has expired.
Attempting to run the application will invoke a dialog allowing you to browse to and apply a new license file (.
GEO will automatically run once the new license has been applied.
If you do not have a license file and wish to request one, please follow the procedure below.
Requesting a Rental Update If you are presented with a dialog box when accessing GEO you license has either expired or close to expiring.
Choose the appropriate option from the warning dialog.
The Request License Renewal E-mail will invoke.
You will see that some information is already pre-filled for you.
All you have to do is supply the dates of your new rental period and fill in your personal/company (license) details.
On receipt of your request we shall provide a response e-mail notifying you that we are dealing with your request.
Opening/Applying a License Update File Locate your.
WibuCmRaU file Click on it so it appears in the File Name section.
Click OK to apply the new license information.
New license Period activated indication will appear.
Should you need to change your computers clock Important.
Usage Information is stored in the RUS dongle using your computers clock.
If changing your machine time is required i. e. you are changing time zones, it is recommended that you use the Time Zones feature accessible through the Windows Ô clock, rather than changing your time manually.
Changing the clock manually will disrupt the time configuration and you may risk losing time on your rental - or worse rendering your licence completely inaccessible.

• Locate your .WibuCmRaU file
• Click on it so it appears in the File Name section.
• Click OK to apply the new license information.
• New license Period activated indication will appear.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Sharing\e-View_Enable_an_ODF.htm =====

e-View Enable an ODF e-View Enable an ODF ↵ e-View Enable an ODF Configuring an ODF to be opened by e-View is the most efficient and cost effective way of sharing your data.
Our free viewer, GEO e-View can be downloaded from our website www.
When an ODF becomes e-View enabled anyone with a copy of e-View can potentially open the file, thus as default all ODF 's are e-view disabled.
To e-View Enable an Document Open the required ODF /ODT
On the Edit tab, select Global Settings.
The Global Settings dialog box will open.
On the Other tab, check the Allow this Document to be opened by Geo e-View (middle of dialog box).
To disable the document, clear this box.
Your document is now e-View enabled.
You can quickly check this by returning to the main GEO window, where at the right hand side of the status bar ‘e-View Enabled’ will be highlighted in light blue.
Adversely when the document is not configured to be viewed by e-View, ‘e-View Disabled’ will appear in gray.
You can quickly enable an ODF to be viewed by e-View by right clicking on the above text on the status bar and selecting ‘ e-View Enabled ’.
To disable an ODF, right-click again and select ‘ e-View Disabled ’.
Auto-Enable It is possible to change the default setting so that all documents are automatically e-View enabled.
On the Edit tab, select Edit GEO Settings.
The GEO Registry Editor will open.
On the General tab, check the Allow New ODF s to be Opened by GEO eView by default (middle right).
Of course you can disable and enable individual documents as you please using the option in Global Settings.

• Open the required ODF/ODT
• On the Edit tab, select Global Settings . The Global Settings dialog box will open.
• On the Other tab, check the Allow this Document to be opened by Geo e-View (middle of dialog box).
• To disable the document, clear this box.
• On the Edit tab, select Edit GEO Settings . The GEO Registry Editor will open.
• On the General tab, check the Allow New ODFs to be Opened by GEOeView by default (middle right).

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Sharing\Event_Log.htm =====

Event Log ↵ Event Log The Event log records important episodes in the life of an ODF file.
File saving, curve editing and loading episodes are all recorded in the View Event Log in Descending Ch ronological order dialog box.
This can be invoked by selecting View Event Log from the GEO tab.
Events are listed in a chronological order, applying a date and time stamp for each.
The following are included in the event log: ODF file load Save OUF creation Log on as a new user name Depth shift the curves Note.
A new save event would not be created every time you save the ODF file.
If one user saved a file multiple times in one day, only one save event would be recorded.
The date and time field would simply update and record the most recent time saved.
The next day however, the first save would invoke a new file save event.
If multiple users saved files multiple times in one day, a save event would be recorded for each user detailing the most recent time saved.
The event log details the following information.
Start and end data depth (relating to the data load event).
The name of the User who logged on to the software at the time of the ‘event’.
Date and time of the ‘event’.
The Error column that details any GEO error ‘message number’ should an error occur during a file load or save episode.
If no error occurs this value will show zero.
This information depends on the ‘event’.
If it were a file load episode for example, the description would detail the ‘Number of data columns that were loaded’, ‘File path’, ‘File name’, ‘ GEO license number’ and whether the curves were appended.
Relating to a file save, the description will detail the directory saved to and the file name.
Click Print to print the event log using the printer that you have setup through the Print Setup.
The user can resize this dialog box, as well as the widths of the data-table columns.
The next time this dialog box is invoked, it will use the last-sized width (also the data-table columns).

• ODF file load
• Save
• OUF creation
• Log on as a new user name
• Depth shift the curves
• Start and end data depth (relating to the data load event).
• The name of the User who logged on to the software at the time of the ‘event’.
• Date and time of the ‘event’.
• The Error column that details any GEO error ‘message number’ should an error occur during a file load or save episode. If no error occurs this value will show zero.
• Description . This information depends on the ‘event’. If it were a file load episode for example, the description would detail the ‘Number of data columns that were loaded’, ‘File path’, ‘File name’, ‘GEO license number’ and whether the curves were appended. Relating to a file save, the description will detail the directory saved to and the file name.

Jumping to a certain depth ↵ Jumping to a certain depth To jump or go to a certain place on your log (either Depth or Time, depends on the defined Plot Index ), on the Depth tab select Index Convert or, or press <CTRL > + < HOME > on your keyboard.
This will open the Convert Index dialog box.
Enter the depth or time of the section of log you wish to view and click Go to.
This will instantly display the relevant depth section and so eradicates the need to scroll through large expanses of log.
Placing your mouse cursor over the scroll-button and then left-clicking and holding, invokes a tool-tip showing the depth currently at the top of the on-screen log.
Dragging the button up or down changes the depth within the tool-tip.
Release the left - mouse button at the required depth, and the on-screen log will re-draw with the selected depth at the top of the screen.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Sharing\Login_for_Access_to_Document.htm =====

Login for Access to Document ↵ Login for Access to Document In order to preserve secrecy on any work that you do within GEO, it is possible for you to set password protection on your files.
There are three levels of protection you can apply to a document: Update, View / Print and Export.
When attempting to access a document that is password protected you will be faced with a drop down option box and a text box.
Select File, then Open/Import to locate the desired document.
Click on the small arrow at the end of the drop down option box.
Select Update, View / Print or Export.
In the box below type in the password for the appropriate selection.
Clicking Cancel will result in the appearance of a warning message and termination of the GEO program.
Once access is granted you may perform the relevant modifications or actions dependent on the access level you have reached.
Any option that is ‘grayed’ out will not be available on the current level of access.
Passwords are not case sensitive.

• Select File , then Open/Import to locate the desired document.
• Click on the small arrow at the end of the drop down option box.
• Select Update , View / Print or Export .
• In the box below type in the password for the appropriate selection.
• Click OK

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Sharing\Protecting_your_ODF_File.htm =====

Protecting your ODF File ↵ Protecting your ODF File ODF files can be password protected should the content of the file be of a confidential nature, and/or you want to prevent certain recipients of the file from modifying or updating its content.
Use the following procedure to password your file.
On the Define tab, select Password s.
The Specify Access for Document will open.
From the Select Desired Access list, select the Update access level.
In the Enter Password for Acc ess, type the chosen password.
Re-confirm the password in the Re-enter Password box.
The password is not case sensitive and its maximum length is 15 characters.
Repeat this process for the View / Print and Export access level listed in the Select desired Access box.
Remember to keep a record of your chosen password(s) in a secure place, as once password protected you will not be able to open the ODF, or change/remove password protection without the correct Update level password.
Next time the ODF file is saved, the password protection will be implemented at the chosen access level.
Each time the ODF file is opened thereafter, the appropriate password must be entered for the required access level.
You cannot apply a password for View / Print access, without first applying a password for Update access.
Password protection can be removed/changed only by opening the ODF with the Update access level password, and then deleting the entries in the password fields.
You must delete the View / Print access password first, before attempting to remove the password for Update access.
If a password for Update access has been applied to an ODF, you basically send it as a ‘Read-Only’ file to another party (or simply like a picture).
The other party will not have any access to the data that builds this ODF, unless they are separately provided with the appropriate password.

• On the Define tab, select Passwords . The Specify Access for Document will open.
• From the Select Desired Access list, select the Update access level.
• In the Enter Password for Acc ess , type the chosen password.
• Re-confirm the password in the Re-enter Password box. Note . The password is not case sensitive and its maximum length is 15 characters.
• Click Update .
• Repeat this process for the View / Print and Export access level listed in the Select desired Access box.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Sharing\Create_a_Report_Link_to_an_Object_in_the_Log\Object_Links_in_GEO.htm =====

Object Links in GEO Object Links in GEO You can provide additional information for log elements (such as lithology units, modifiers, symbols, free format text and track text blocks) by linking those objects, at any instance within the log, with another file (e. g. a morning-report that is written in MS Word Ô format).
When viewing the log ( ODF ) within a web browser (such as Internet Explorer Ô ), the link feature will allow the user to click an object and read any further information that is linked to it.
This allows you to create ‘hyperlinks’ as they are widely deployed throughout the internet or on intranets, without any prior knowledge of the web-based Hyper-Text Markup Language
In GEO, an object can have an External Link, an Internal Link, or both.
External Links Typically an External Link could point to a Universal Resource Locator [URL] (on the Internet or Intranet) or Network location that provides more information about one of the above objects.
This information is not stored in the document, only a link to the information is stored.
The Link could point to a Web page, a picture or other document.
For example a Core symbol could point to a URL that has an actual picture of the core section stored on the Intranet or Internet.
This allows information to be stored at the most appropriate location, where it can be kept up-to-date and easily viewed from the Link in your document.
Internal Links An Internal Link can be used to associate a Header or Trailer specifications with a lithology, symbol or free format text occurrence.
Learn how to add a header or trailer to your log.
Create or Modify links Right-click the object on the log that you want to link to another report (or photograph, etc.).
Click Create/ Modify Link from the menu.
The Create or Modify Ext ernal and Internal Links for an Object dialog box will open.
Create or modify an External Link by typing in the desired URL or using the Browse button to locate a local or network file.
Create or modify an Internal Link by selecting the corresponding header or trailer option button and selecting the appropriate specification.
Alternatively, clicking Links from the properties dialog box of each object also allows you to create or modify the links.
This option allows you to truncate any file path relative to the location of the actual log you are linking the object too.
If the file path of the linked document is the same as the log then the path will be truncated to ‘.\ Core Data.
doc’ for example, denoting its location as the same as the log itself.
Left clear, the file path will be displayed in UNC ( Universal Naming Convention ).
Viewing the links If an object has an Internal or External Link, its location is displayed in a tool tip when the mouse pointer is over the object.
You can open that external link by right-clicking the object and clicking Open External Link from the menu.
This should invoke your web browser for a Web URL, or an application associated with whatever the external link references (for example, a link to a file with a. doc extension would normally open MS Word Ô, if this application is present on the viewing-user’s computer or network).
For an internal link, click Go after right-clicking the object, to bring the referenced header or trailer into view.
Markers You can select a more obvious indicator that a link exists by selecting a mark from the drop down list at the bottom of the dialog box.
The adjacent drop down list the positions you can display your marker.
To remove an unwanted marker, simply set the marker to the blank option at the top of the list.
The In Use option is automatically checked when you create a link, defining the link as active.
In order to delete a link, clear this option, the link will then be deleted.
Additional Information ODF viewers like GEO View and GEO e-View do not have context menus for objects (i. e. you cannot right-click the object).
However, if an object has a link, this is displayed as a tool tip when the mouse pointer is above it, and the mouse pointer should change to the pointing-hand form, indicating the presence of the link.
In addition, double-clicking on the object will bring an Internal Link into view or invoke the appropriate action for an External Link.
If the object has both an Internal and an External Link, a context menu will display to allow selection of the appropriate link.
SVG output also contains External link information and may be viewed by double clicking the object.
If an object has a link, when the mouse pointer is brought over the object in the SVG display, the mouse pointer should also change to a hand pointer and display link information in the status bar of the Web browser.
Learn how to export the plot to SVG format.

• Right-click the object on the log that you want to link to another report (or photograph, etc.).
• Click Create/Modify Link from the menu. The Create or Modify Ext ernal and Internal Links for an Object dialog box will open. Create or modify an External Link by typing in the desired URL or using the Browse button to locate a local or network file. Create or modify an Internal Link by selecting the corresponding header or trailer option button and selecting the appropriate specification.
• Create or modify an External Link by typing in the desired URL or using the Browse button to locate a local or network file.
• Create or modify an Internal Link by selecting the corresponding header or trailer option button and selecting the appropriate specification.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Sharing\Export_Data_and_Information\Export_All_Other_Data_(except_curve_data).htm =====

Export All Other Data (except curve data)
Export All Other Data (except curve data)
Export All Other Data (except curve data)
Some of the information used to create a composite log may need to be cataloged in other systems such as the corporate geological database.
Therefore, there should be a means to export data captured by GEO (and encapsulated in the ODF ) to the other system.
There are a couple of ways to do this.
To export all other data, except for the curve data, using the Export All Information feature.
To export the curve data to LAS, Text-tab delimited or Comma-tab delimited format, please use the Export Curve Data feature Export All Information
This feature allows you to select specific ODF components (or objects) to be exported from GEO, since not all objects in an ODF may need to be exported.
For example, although a box around text is a symbol, it has no relevance to geology.
Similarly, in a long sequence the age-dating column may have the word JURASSIC repeated several times.
Only one of the text blocks signifies the correct interval.
This dialog box shows total number of the items in an ODF file and allows you to choose what to be exported from GEO.
Use the following procedure to export the data from GEO through an intermediary text-form file: Open the ODF containing the data to be exported.
On the Export tab select All Info.
The Select Items to Export will open.
Objects with the check box selected will be exported.
If you do not want to export an object, clear the check box.
At each object, you will see the total number of that item in the ODF and the number of selected elements to be exported.
By default, all total numbers will be exported.
Clicking Select at each item brings up the items’ list, allowing you to select a particular item of that object to be exported.
The total number of the selected items of each object will be written under the Selected column.
The Export As dialog box will open.
Enter a File name and select a folder to save to.
Click Save to start exporting the selected objects from GEO.
The ‘logical block’ of the text ( TXT ) file as the Export All Info result is shown below.
A semicolon (";") as the first token in a line denotes a comment-line, which has been inserted only for the purpose of readability.
Each block begins with a BEGIN keyword, followed by the type of the block; a block always ends with an END keyword.
The Global block is always the first block in the file.
The depth values will always be represented in the fixed-point notation.
The mnemonic-name will always be four characters long.
The symbol-type, modifier-type and litho-type will be the (up to) eight-character names as they appear in GEO.
The free-format text and track text field will consist of a text-length field followed by a ":" character and then the text-value.
A single <CR> character denotes a new-line.
Here is an example of the ‘logical block’ format of a TXT file, as am Export All Info result.
units Feet | Meters depth.
range <start-depth> <end-depth> END Global ; NOTE: Several 'Table' blocks are possible!!
BEGIN Table <table-name> <table-id> <depth> <symbol-type> <*field-name> <*field-value>.
END Table BEGIN Mnemonics <mnemonic-name> <*description> <*value>
END Mnemonics BEGIN FreeFormatText <depth> length:<*text>.
END FreeFormatText BEGIN Symbols <symbol-type> <depth>
END Symbols Begin Lithos <litho-type> <start-depth> <end-depth>.
End Lithos BEGIN Modifiers <modifier-type> <depth>
END Modifiers BEGIN CommentText <depth> <length>:<*text>.
END CommentText BEGIN AgeingColumns <start-depth> <end-depth> <*text>.

• To export all other data, except for the curve data, using the Export All Information feature. This is explained below.
• Open the ODF containing the data to be exported.
• On the Export tab select All Info . The Select Items to Export will open.
• Objects with the check box selected will be exported. If you do not want to export an object, clear the check box.
• At each object, you will see the total number of that item in the ODF and the number of selected elements to be exported. By default, all total numbers will be exported.
• Clicking Select at each item brings up the items’ list, allowing you to select a particular item of that object to be exported. The total number of the selected items of each object will be written under the Selected column.
• Click Export . The Export As dialog box will open.
• Enter a File name and select a folder to save to.
• Click Save to start exporting the selected objects from GEO.
• A semicolon (";") as the first token in a line denotes a comment-line, which has been inserted only for the purpose of readability.
• Each block begins with a BEGIN keyword, followed by the type of the block; a block always ends with an END keyword.
• The Global block is always the first block in the file.
• The depth values will always be represented in the fixed-point notation.
• The mnemonic-name will always be four characters long.
• The symbol-type, modifier-type and litho-type will be the (up to) eight-character names as they appear in GEO.
• The free-format text and track text field will consist of a text-length field followed by a ":" character and then the text-value. A single <CR> character denotes a new-line.

Export Curve Data ↵ Export Curve Data
This feature allows curve data to be exported from GEO in three different ASCII formats: LAS file Text Tab-delimited ASCII file Text Comma-delimited ASCII file For full flexibility a fourth format is also available XML (extensible Markup Language) format.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Sharing\Export_Data_and_Information\Export_Curve_Data_to_XML_Format.htm =====

Export Curve Data to XML Format Export Curve Data to XML Format XML (eXtensible Markup Language) is a platform-independent meta-markup language that provides a format for describing structured data.
XML provides a structural representation of data that has proved broadly implementable and easy to deploy across all platforms.
The specifications of XML have been laid down by the World Wide Web Consortium (W3C, see www.
w3c. org for details), an international consortium founded in 1994 to develop standards for the Web.
WellLogML is an XML standard adopted by the Petrotechnical Open Software Corporation (POSC) to exchange well log data (see www.
SDC Geologix is a full member of POSC and collaborates in the development of these standards.
WellLogML is a system for encoding well information for the Web that is flexible and extensible, suitable for interaction with external software on any platform.
WellLogML is similar to LAS, in that it specifies how well log data is organized in terms of Well Information, Curve Information, Parameter Information, etc.
Export Curve Data as XML On the Export tab, select Export Curves.
The Export Curve Data dialog box will open.
In Export Format, select XML.
Select one or more curves to export Note.
These curves MUST have the same depth interval.
Change the Start Depth, End Depth and Null Value if necessary.
Choose the appropriate value for the Parameter Information from and the W e ll Information from.
Click Export, choose a folder and file-name to export to and click Save.

• On the Export tab, select Export Curves . The Export Curve Data dialog box will open.
• In Export Format , select XML .
• Select one or more curves to export Note . These curves MUST have the same depth interval.
• Change the Start Depth , End Depth and Null Value if necessary.
• Choose the appropriate value for the Parameter Information from and the W e ll Information from .
• Click Export , choose a folder and file-name to export to and click Save .

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Sharing\Export_Data_and_Information\Export_Data_to_WitsML.htm =====

Export Data to WitsML Export Data to WitsML WitsML is an information transfer standard based on XML technology that has no set platform and is language independent, making it wholly flexible for the range of data that can be attained from a well.
There are six types of data you may export from an ODF /ODT:
Mudlog Object encapsulates Geological information such as Gas data, descriptions, lithology, % lithology, table/curve parameter details and now qualitative information.
Wellbore Geometry Exclusively deals with casing/borehole table data.
Formation Marker Deals with sequence/formation top table data.
Tubular Used to export data related to the BHA and drillstring.
Log Object Deals with curve data, a single Log object can harbor multiple curves.
If you have the export modules as part of your GEO Licence you can access the Export wizard from the Export tab, and select Create Text Output Profile.

Mudlog Object | encapsulates Geological information such as Gas data, descriptions, lithology, % lithology, table/curve parameter details and now qualitative information.
Wellbore Geometry | Exclusively deals with casing/borehole table data.
Trajectory | Collects survey data.
Formation Marker | Deals with sequence/formation top table data.
Tubular | Usedto export data related to the BHA and drillstring.
Log Object | Deals with curve data, a single Log object can harbor multiple curves.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Sharing\Export_Data_and_Information\Export_to_Image_File\Export_GEO_Plot_as_Image.htm =====

Export GEO Plot as Image Export GEO Plot as Image There are multiple options for the conversion of your plot into an image format.
Metafiles are essentially a way of intelligently storing pictorial information and provide a useful means of transferring plots to other applications.
Their main advantage is that in general, they are far less prone to distortion when scaled than bitmaps.
This is because in a metafile, shapes can be defined as a mathematical formula rather than as a conglomeration of dots.
The other advantage is that a metafile usually requires less disk space than a corresponding bitmap.
You can export the complete plot, or any section of it, to the following formats.
CGM - Computer Graphics Metafiles (Binary format) WMF - Standard Windows Metafile Placeable WMF WMF - Metafile Picture to Clipboard EMF - Enhanced Metafile EMF - Enhanced Metafile using Screen Settings EMF - Enhanced Metafile to clipboard TIFF - Tagged Image Format SVG - Scaleable Vector Graphics Export Plot as an Image On the Export tab, select Export As.
then select the image format you wish to export to.
If saving to clipboard, for example EMF to Clipboard, you can now paste it into another application.
Enter a File name and path where the output will be stored.
The default path for these exported files depends on the type of metafile output selected.
The default path for WMF and CGM are defined at the File Locations tab in the Registry Editor dialog box (opened by selecting Edit GEO Settings from the Edit tab) and can be changed, as required.
Prior to exporting to a metafile, select a suitable printer device from the print setup dialog box.
GEO will use the device driver to obtain the horizontal resolution (pixels per inch), vertical resolution (pixels per inch), page size (pixels) and text formatting information.
We recommend you install a suitable printer driver for just this purpose, as our experience has shown that certain printer-drivers are poor at creating metafiles.
We recommend use of the printer-driver for the EPSON STYLUS 1520 COLOR Ô printer for optimum metafile creation.

• EMF - Enhanced Metafile using Screen Settings
• EMF - Enhanced Metafile to clipboard

Export GEO Plot to CGM Export GEO Plot to CGM The CGM (Computer Graphic Metafile) format can be used to transfer a plot to a large plotter (e. g. HP DesignJet Ô ) through CGM interpreter software (such as Zeh Graphics Ô or SDI Ô software).
One reason for doing so is to circumvent the length limitation (109 inches) of certain printer-drivers operating under Windows Ô.
This limitation does not of course arise when plotting under the UNIX platform.
GEO can export to CGM files with either 16 or 32-bit precision.
The 16-bit CGM complies with ISO-8362 binary specifications and may not be able to cope with very long plots.
The 32-bit CGM, on the other hand, is equipped to handle any length of plot and is compatible with PIP (Petroleum Information Profile).
Export Plot to CGM On the Edit tab, select Headers and Trailers.
T he Plot Header and Trailer Specifications dialog box will open.
If a trailer component such as a spreadsheet was loaded with the OLE object check box selected, you can remove the OLE object with the following simple procedure.
Double-click that spreadsheet in the trailer in GEO to open it in the native application (perhaps MS Excel Ô ).
Copy it to the clipboard and load it back at the Plot Header and Trailer Specifications dialog box, with the same name, but this time ensure the OLE object check box is clear (no tick).
On the Edit tab, select Edit GEO Settings.
The Registry Editor dialog box will open.
Open the CGM Advanced tab and check the settings.
The defaults are usually good in most cases.
On the Export tab, select Export as.
The Export to CGM (32 bit) will open.
Enter the File name and specify the path to save to.
For output to the plotter, such as the HP DesignJet Ô series transfer the corresponding CGM format and its parameter file (with par extension) to the plotter by using FTP ( File Transfer Protocol) to the UNIX platform.

Export GEO Plot to SVG Export GEO Plot to SVG Scalable Vector Graphics ( SVG ) is an open standard vector graphics language.
It is XML -based and can be used for Web graphics.
The World Wide Web Consortium (W3C) maintains the SVG specification.
Export plot to SVG On the Depth tab, enter the Index Range you wish to export in From and To.
On the Export tab, select Export as.
then SVG - Scaleable Vector Graphics.
An Export To dialog box will open.
Enter a File name and the directory where it is going to be stored.
The following video selects WMF as the export format.
Simply replace this selection with SVG.
The resulting XML file (with extension.
SVG ) complies with the SVG specification and can be viewed by SVG viewers.
The SVG file can also be embedded in a web page and viewed in a web browser that has the appropriate plug-in to view SVG.
Since the SVG file uses a clear text representation to describe graphical information, the size of the generated file may be large depending on the length and density of graphical information present in your section of displayed log.
In addition to the graphical output, SVG hotspots are generated for items that have links in the document.
If you view the generated SVG file in a browser (such as Internet Explorer Ô ), the items with links (e. g. a core symbol) will have a hotspot.
When your mouse is over such an item in your web browser, the mouse pointer will change to a hand and double-clicking should take you to the linked item.
In the following example, a reference to a generated SVG file e:\temp\test.
svg has been embedded into an HTML page.
The height and width should correspond to the size of the graphic image in the SVG file.
This is especially useful for efficient scrolling of relatively long sections of log in a Web browser.
svg" NAME=" SVG Embed" TYPE="image/svg-xml" PLUGINSPAGE="http://www. adobe.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Sharing\Export_Data_and_Information\Export_to_Image_File\Export_GEO_Plot_to_TIFF.htm =====

Export GEO Plot to TIFF Export GEO Plot to TIFF The TIFF export option can be used to replicate the GEO plot in to a commonly used graphics format.
This file can then be viewed within many third party graphics applications.
The TIFF feature can be used to export the plot as a whole, however for large plots, in both width and length there are some associated limits to be aware of.
There are two controls for exporting to TIFF format - DPI and Page Height.
Both of these options can be edited on the Edit tab in Edit GEO Settings ( General tab).
DPI DPI or Dots per Inch, relates to the resolution and quality of the output.
The higher the DPI the better quality the image will be.
When an ODF is viewed on screen at 100% please bear in mind that this will be approximately 96dpi, thus increasing the DPI for TIFF export will also serve to increase the respective size of the image by that factor.
The page height relates to the maximum length in pixels of your TIFF page.
If your log exceeds 2048 pixels wide then your max page height will be 32000 pixels If your log is less than 2048 pixels wide then your max page height will be 64000 pixels Therefore if your log is longer than 64/32k pixels then you will output a multi-page TIFF file.
Export to TIFF On the Depth tab, enter the Index Range you wish to export in From and To.
On the Export tab, select Export As.
then TIFF Tagged Image Format.
The Export To Tiff File As dialog box will open.
Browse to save location and enter a file name.
The following video selects WMF as the export format.
Simply replace this selection with TIFF.
If you experience memory issues during this process, try reducing the DPI.

• DPI DPI or Dots per Inch, relates to the resolution and quality of the output. The higher the DPI the better quality the image will be. When an ODF is viewed on screen at 100% please bear in mind that this will be approximately 96dpi, thus increasing the DPI for TIFF export will also serve to increase the respective size of the image by that factor.

If your log exceeds 2048 pixels wide then your max page height will be 32000 pixels If your log is less than 2048 pixels wide then your max page height will be 64000 pixels Therefore if your log is longer than 64/32k pixels then you will output a multi-page TIFF file.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Sharing\ODF_Update_File_(OUF))\Concept_of_ODF_Update_File_(OUF).htm =====

Concept of ODF Update File ( OUF ) Concept of ODF Update File ( OUF ) ↵ ↵
Concept of ODF Update File ( OUF )
The ODF Update File or OUF, which was introduced with version 4 of GEO Software, enables you to send daily updates with a high level of security, very cost effectively.
The prime purposes are: Adding security when e-mailing files: This is because the OUF files must be loaded sequentially.
Reducing the size, and therefore cost, of e-mailing daily updates over expensive satellite links.
The OUF file only carries ‘Update’ information; as a result the size of the files is reduced substantially.
While an ODF is being created at the wellsite, the size and complexity of the file increases throughout the duration of the well, as progressively more data is added to it.
The security of mailing the file becomes increasingly important, as do the actual costs involved.
In the scenario where a wellsite user e-mails files to an operations base, the sending of the entire ODF on a daily basis can become inefficient.
This is especially true when the recipient of the ODF is only concerned with the updates.
In the OUF model, the Wellsite user creates and maintains a Parent ODF.
From this sequential OUF files are saved.
These files are then mailed to the operations base and loaded to build an identical Child ODF.
The OUF files must be loaded in the correct sequence to successfully build the Child ODF.
The scenario below attempts to show the best practice on how this OUF model may be conducted.
At the Wellsite The first time the ODF is saved, you simply select Save
As from the GEO menu and supply a file name as normal.
When the first transfer of data from the wellsite to operations base is required, you would simply select Save OUF Updates from the GEO menu (or Send OUF Update Via Mail if you are going to send the file directly through an e-mail facility already present and set up in your PC – requires internet connection).
GEO takes the file name supplied and creates the first OUF file.
You would then e-mail, disk-fax or modem transfer the ‘WellX- 001.
ouf ’ to the operations base, instead of the WellX. odf.
Because of its in-built compressibility, the resultant OUF file will always be smaller than the Parent ODF, although for the very first transmission, there probably will not be such a marked difference in file sizes as is noticeable with the subsequent OUF s. Between transfers, the wellsite user can of course keep the Parent ODF up-to-date and saved on the local drive by using the normal Save procedure from the GEO menu.
For the next transfer, you would again select Save OUF Updates or Send OUF Update Via Mail.
GEO will then save this update as an OUF, called WellX-002.
ouf will simultaneously save the WellX. odf to the same point.
If you select Save As instead of Save OUF Updates it would result in a GEO warning message (840) advising you that saving the ODF to another name would break the connection between this ODF and all subsequent OUF s’.
Hence, say if the ODF was saved under a different name e. g. WellZ. odf.
The next time you go to Save OUF Updates the OUF would revert to WellZ- 001.
ouf because of the name change.
All the information loaded would then be encapsulated in this new OUF under the newly named ODF.
At the Operations Base You have two options for loading the OUF file.
Double-clicking on the OUF e-mail attachment.
This would launch GEO and load the OUF file automatically.
Detaching the e-mail attachment and selecting Load OUF Updates from the GEO menu After loading the 001.
ouf, the file must be saved as an ODF.
You can give a file name as appropriate.
The ODF created is often called the ‘Child’ ODF.
Each time an OUF is received and loaded, the ODF is saved prior to loading subsequent OUF s.
This ensures the child ODF is at the correct stage to load the next OUF in sequence.
The OUF s must be loaded in sequence.
If the wellsite user accidentally sends 004.
ouf without previously sending 003.
ouf the operations base user cannot load the file.
This is an important security element of the OUF file.
Please note, that OUF files may be opened and viewed within the full viewer application, GEO View.
OUF files cannot be opened directly using the free viewer, GEO e-View.
Files must first be consolidated within an ODF file (using GEO or GEO View).
After the ODF has been e-View enabled (using GEO ), it may only then be freely shared with users of the GEO e-View application.
In addition to the GEO Plus application, OUF files may be opened and viewed within the full viewer application, GEO View.
OUF files cannot be opened directly using the free viewer, GEO e-View.
Files must first be consolidated within an ODF file (using GEO or GEO View ).
After the ODF has been e-View enabled (using GEO ), it may only then be freely shared with users of the GEO e-View application.
What happens if the OUF connection is broken?
Any amendments made in the PARENT ODF, and the OUF subsequently created, will over-ride changes made in the Child ODF.
The Replication Information dialog box serves to advise the operations base user, if an amendment made in the Child ODF, has also been changed in the OUF they are loading.
This is the only scenario where a Replication Information dialog box is invoked detailing a Replication Conflict.
Example: The operations base user loads an OUF.
They then move a casing shoe symbol from 4000ft to 4500ft, and save the child ODF.
The next OUF received includes the same casing shoe having been moved in the PARENT ODF from 4000ft to 4250ft.
When the operations base user loads this OUF they will first see a Replication Information dialog box.
This advises the operations base user that a change made to the child ODF has also been changed in the parent ODF.
Exiting the dialog box will over-write the change made by the operations user in the child ODF.
After loading this OUF the casing shoe will be moved to 4250ft.
GEO takes the OUF to be loaded and checks the contents of this OUF against the contents of the child ODF.
In the above example, the Replication Information dialog box would not have been produced if the symbol had not been moved in the PARENT ODF.
The child ODF can be altered any number of times without invoking the ‘Replication Conflict’, as long as an alteration using the same log object has not been implemented in the parent ODF.
Further Example: A sandstone block has two pyritic modifiers at 3000ft. GEO assigns these modifiers their own unique id numbers (e. g. 20 & 21).
The child ODF is altered, by shifting modifier 20 to 2995ft and then saved.
The PARENT ODF is altered, by shifting modifier 21 to 3005ft.
The next sequential OUF is then saved.
When this OUF is loaded into the child ODF, a Replication Information dialog box will not open.
If however, in a later OUF, modifier 20 is shifted from 3000ft to 3005ft, upon loading this OUF a Replication Information dialog box is opened.
This is because the OUF records the shift from 3000ft to 3005ft in the parent ODF.
When scanning the child ODF, GEO by default, assumes the modifier to be positioned at 3000ft but upon loading the OUF scans and records the same modifier (20), positioned at 2995ft.
This ‘deviation’ invokes the Replication Information dialog box.

• Adding security when e-mailing files: This is because the OUF files must be loaded sequentially.
• Reducing the size, and therefore cost, of e-mailing daily updates over expensive satellite links.
• The OUF file only carries ‘Update’ information; as a result the size of the files is reduced substantially.
• Double-clicking on the OUF e-mail attachment. This would launch GEO and load the OUF file automatically.
• Detaching the e-mail attachment and selecting Load OUF Updates from the GEO menu

Create or Save an OUF ↵ Create or Save an OUF Save an ODF file in the normal way by clicking Save As from the GEO menu.
Create an OUF file from that ODF by selecting Save OUF Updates from GEO menu.
Any amendments in the ODF file can then be saved into OUF format by selecting Save OUF Update from GEO menu.
This at the same time will save the ODF file.
Alternatively, if your e-mail software has been setup, click Send OUF updates via Mail from the GEO menu.
This method also creates an OUF file with a sequentially-numbered file name, and in addition incorporates the OUF into an e-mail as the correctly named file-attachment.
Do not rename OUF files.
GEO gives the OUF the same filename as its PARENT ODF together with its sequence number.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Sharing\ODF_Update_File_(OUF))\Load_OUF_Files.htm =====

Load OUF Files ↵ Load OUF Files Upon receiving an OUF file, load the file either by detaching the e-mail attachments or by selecting Load OUF Updates from the GEO menu.
Locate the OUF file and Open.
Save the file as an ODF file in the normal way (click Save As from the GEO menu).
This saves the ‘Child’ ODF onto your machine.
Repeat these steps to load the sequential incoming OUF files and save them into one ODF file to create the local replica (or child) of the PARENT ODF.

• Upon receiving an OUF file, load the file either by detaching the e-mail attachments or by selecting Load OUF Updates from the GEO menu.
• Locate the OUF file and Open .
• Save the file as an ODF file in the normal way (click Save As from the GEO menu). This saves the ‘Child’ ODF onto your machine.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Sharing\ODF_Update_File_(OUF))\OUF_Auto_merging.htm =====

OUF Auto merge ↵ OUF Auto merge The Auto merge OUF feature allows users to load OUF files received (from wellsite or well partner) at a user-defined frequency (or time interval).
This frequency can be set by entering the appropriate value (in minutes) at A uto Merge OUF s every box at the Other tab of Global Settings dialog box (on the Edit tab).
The feature is disabled by default as the frequency is set at 0 (zero) minutes.
To enable the feature, simply specify the frequency at which the application should ‘check’ for new OUF files to auto-merge into the child ODF.
An OUF Load directory must be specified from the File Locations tab of the Registry Editor dialog box.
This dialog box can be launched from GEO by selecting Edit GEO Settings from the Edit tab.
At the user-defined frequency specified, the application reverts to the location specified for the OUF Load Directory to check for the new OUF files.
The procedure is as follows: Load the first OUF file by clicking Load OUF Updates from the GEO menu.
Once the first OUF has been loaded, you must save it as an ODF file.
From this point, the software will revert to the folder location specified, at the user-defined frequency, to check for and load the next sequential OUF file(s).
If the next expected file is present in the OUF Load folder, and the relevant ODF file open, the software will confirm whether you wish to load that sequential OUF.
If multiple sequential OUF files are encountered, these can be loaded in turn.
If the frequency of transmission of OUF files from the wellsite is increased, if only to match the realistic acquisition of data, then this feature may be deployed to provide an often operationally satisfactory ‘near-real time’ data stream to the operations base.

• Load the first OUF file by clicking Load OUF Updates from the GEO menu.
• Once the first OUF has been loaded, you must save it as an ODF file.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Sharing\ODF_Update_File_(OUF))\OUF_Resave_Feature.htm =====

OUF Resave Feature ↵ OUF
Resave Feature What happens if somehow the chain of OUF file is broken (for instance, lost during sending) and cannot be re-sent?
There is an OUF re-save feature that enables the parent OUF user to re-save over previously saved OUF s. Example: The wellsite user saves 007.
ouf after loading new data.
This data happens to be corrupt and upon mailing, the recipient experiences difficulty loading the OUF.
When the 007 is re-sent, the same problem occurs again so the well site user becomes aware of the problem.
The corrupt data is stripped from the ODF, and new data is reloaded.
You select Save OUF Updates from the GEO menu and GEO saves the OUF as 008.
This OUF cannot be loaded by the user in the operation base, since the last OUF loaded successfully was 006 and the OUF s must be loaded in sequence.
The wellsite user can click Resave Range of OUF Updates from the GEO menu and select the 007.
ouf from the list in the Description column of the dialog box.
Clicking Save will create a 007_009.
The 007_ portion of this filename is created because the operations user must have a 007.
ouf to maintain the sequence.
The _009 portion is created because the wellsite user created a 008.
This must now be by-passed since the 008.
ouf required the original 007.
The next OUF created by the wellsite user will be 010.
The operations user will be able to load this 010.
ouf because the last OUF loaded was the 007_009.
ouf and the _009 portion of this OUF maintains the sequence.
If an OUF sequence is ever broken, for any reasons, the Resave Range of OUF Updates option from the GEO menu can be utilized to successfully re-establish the link.
If the recipient user accidentally deleted the child ODF and the constituent OUF s, the link could always be re-established as long as the parent ODF exists.
In an extreme scenario, the wellsite user, after saving 1000 OUF s could click Re-Save Range of OUF Updates and select number 001.
ouf from the dialog box list.
GEO would then create a 001_1001.
ouf, which would include every well data amendment and addition in those 1000 OUF s. This could be e-mailed to the operations base user, loaded, and saved as a new child ODF.
The next OUF saved by the wellsite user will be 1002.
The operations base user could then load this OUF without any problem.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Sharing\ODF_Update_File_(OUF))\Send_OUF_as_mail_attachment.htm =====

Send OUF as mail attachment ↵ Send OUF as Mail Attachment
In most cases, the OUF will be sent from one place to another as an e-mail attachment.
There are two ways to place the OUF as an e-mail attachment:
By attaching the OUF files manually within your e-mail software itself.
Using Send OUF Updates via Mail (from the GEO menu) feature in GEO.
If the Send OUF Updates via Mail feature is utilized, you do not need to click the Save OUF Updates to save the sequential OUF.
Pointing at Send OUF Updates via Mail and clicking the Updates option automatically saves the next sequential OUF file.
For first time usage, you need to go through the following procedure to set it up: On the GEO meny, select Send OUF Updates via Mail to open the Choose Profile dialog box.
It allows you to select the information service by which the OUF file will be mailed.
You can set up your choice of information service using the Windows Messaging Set-Up Wizard.
Once selected, this invokes your installed e-mail software (for example MS Outlook) and opens the Message dialog box.
The Message dialog box consists of two tabs - Message and Options.
The Message tab allows you to enter the address (or addresses) of the OUF recipient(s).
You can enter any desired text here, which is then mailed along with the OUF file.
The Options tab allows you to set several options relating to the conditions under which the mail is sent.
The Importance Level, Delivery Options and Tracking Options can all be set from this tab.
Next time you click Send OUF Updates via Mail from the GEO menu, the corresponding OUF will be saved and it will open your e-mail software with the OUF automatically created as the attachment.
You can type the message as normal prior to sending this e-mail.
In the event that you not complete the Send OUF via Mail sequence and quit partially through the steps (e. g. you do not really send the e-mail), GEO will inform you that the OUF file has already been saved (specifying the file path) and that the particular OUF must be sent manually (as an e-mail attachment, for example).
If you click Send Range of OUF Updates via Mail, a Re-Save range of updates dialog box opens.
Click the row which details the OUF sequence number to be saved over.
Click Save and this will create an underscore OUF number that can be sent as an e-mail attachment.

• By attaching the OUF files manually within your e-mail software itself.
• Using Send OUF Updates via Mail (from the GEO menu) feature in GEO.
• On the GEO meny, select Send OUF Updates via Mail to open the Choose Profile dialog box. It allows you to select the information service by which the OUF file will be mailed. You can set up your choice of information service using the Windows Messaging Set-Up Wizard. Once selected, this invokes your installed e-mail software (for example MS Outlook) and opens the Message dialog box.
• The Message dialog box consists of two tabs - Message and Options . The Message tab allows you to enter the address (or addresses) of the OUF recipient(s) . You can enter any desired text here, which is then mailed along with the OUF file. The Options tab allows you to set several options relating to the conditions under which the mail is sent. The Importance Level, Delivery Options and Tracking Options can all be set from this tab.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Sharing\Publish_ODF_to_Web_Folder\VUF_File_Transfe.htm =====

VUF File Transfer VUF File Transfer With the VUF feature it is possible to transfer ODF files quickly, efficiently and in real time between remote locations via an Internet connection.
This feature is also used to publish the ODF into a web folder.
The ODF is divided into multiple VUF files based on chunk size (in pixels), which are compressed during the saving process and then published to a web folder.
The VUF files can then be streamed in, in a sequential manner, decompressing as they do.
Stream Out Click File from the GEO menu bar and select Stream Out VUF s; a dialog box will appear.
Enter the FULL URL for the Web folder directory or path for the File directory that you want to store the VUF files in.
Enter a Chunk Size in pixels (i. e. the amount of pixels you wish to be in each separate VUF file).
Selecting one of the Chunks Ordered option buttons allows you to select the sequence that the files are saved in, e. g. descending (bottom of log to top) or ascending (top of log to bottom).
Define what chunk you want to save the headers and trailers in (e. g. chunk one, two or at the end) by selecting the appropriate option button.
Select Save to publish the file, or Cancel to abort.
Stream In Open GEO (or GEO View or GEO e-View ) and click File from the menu bar and select Stream In VUF s. Enter the FULL URL for the Web folder directory or path for the File directory, followed by the file name of the VUF files Note.
Name of first VUF file will be the ODF file name succeeded by ‘-001. vuf’ Select OK to begin streaming in, or Cancel to abort.
Large graphics in the headers and trailers will significantly decrease streaming speeds.
The bigger the chunk size in pixels, the longer it will take the first file to stream in, however a bigger chunk size will generate less chunks, thus total time may be slightly decreased.
As a guide we recommend a chunk size of approx 800 pixels.

Yes, No or Cancel as required.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Working_with_Files\Files_in_GEO.htm =====

File s in GEO File s in GEO File s reside in directories located on the in-use disk, where they are identified by their names.
By default, GEO files reside in the following location (unless formatted differently on installation).
Example ODF files C:\Users\*username*\Documents\MyWells Example Templates C:\Users\*username*\AppData\Roaming\SDC Software\Geo Suite 8\Geo\Templates File names are in the form of a name (given by a user) and an extension specific to the file type.
The name can be up to 255 characters long (including the space and path names), while the extension (after the period [.]) is usually 3 characters long.
The File menu is used to control file related activities such as opening, closing and saving files as well as printing and loading data, or importing %lithology from an ASCII file.

• Example Templates C:\Users\*username*\AppData\Roaming\SDC Software\Geo Suite 8\Geo\Templates

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Working_with_Files\File_Types_Handled_by_GEO.htm =====

File Types Handled by GEO File Types Handled by GEO FILE TYPE EXTENSION DESCRIPTION LOAD EXPORT LIS-79 LIS, TAP, NTI, TIF LIS data (usually wireline data) is converted to an ASCII format called LAS before loading into GEO.
There are different kinds of LIS, which are supported by the LIS- LAS Converter routine
No No Canadian Well Log ASCII (CW LAS ) LAS Data_load This is a special ASCII implementation of wireline data that allows for specific categories of information to coexist with data.
GEO can load LAS data directly.
Yes Yes Text ( ASCII ) ASC, TXTData_load Mudlog, MWD and well test data are usually in the Text File format.
Sometimes, the data is presented in columns which are delimited by SPACES.
Such Text files MUST be prepared (externally or within GEO before they can be loaded to the ODF database.
Yes Comma Separated Values ( ASCII ) CSVData_load Some service companies present mudlog data as comma separated values.
Spreadsheets such as Excel and Lotus 123 can also create output in comma separated values format.
This data can be directly read by GEO.
Yes Tab Delimited ( ASCII ) TXTData_load One form of ASCII formats.
Tab delimited files are also created when data is saved as a ‘Text file’ in spreadsheet applications.
This kind of data can be directly read by GEO.
Yes Metafile CGM Export_ CGM
The ISO-8632 implementation of Computer Graphics Metafile.
This popular format can be used to plot to plotters such as Versatec or HP Design Jets.
It is limited by the size of the plot.
No Yes Windows Metafile WMFExport_WMF Both placeable and standard Windows Metafiles are supported.
This is an easy way of getting graphical information to (and from) other applications such as Word and Excel.
Enhanced Metafile EMFExport_EMF Enhanced Metafiles are supported.
This is another way of getting graphical information to (and from) other applications such as Word and Excel.
Yes Scalable Vector Graphics SVG Export_
SVG SVG is a language for describing two-dimensional graphics in XML ( XML -10).
SVG allows for three types of graphic objects: vector graphic shapes (e. g., paths consisting of straight lines and curves), images and text.
Yes Extensible Mark-up Language XML Export_ XML
The Extensible Markup Language ( XML ) is the universal format for structured documents and data on the Web.
Geologix, as a full member of the Petrotechnical Open Software Corporation [POSC] has been instrumental in defining the WellPlotML and WellLogML definitions.
No No VIEW VEW The View file contains the layout-related settings needed to create a log.
These settings are normally entered by the user and may be stored for ease of recall when the same layout is required for subsequent well logs i. e. the standard composite log presentation.
Yes Yes Output Database File ODF The Output Database File is a database where the wireline, mudlog or any other imported data, together with the layout-related View information and the Interpretation-related data is stored.
The ODF enables the rapid recall of all data relating to a particular well, either for further editing/update or for the production of further logs.
No No ODF Database Template ODT File that is created from an ODF with all required components, such as headers, tables, & lithology and then saved as a template in GEO.
No No ODF Interval File OIF These files are concerned with only a specific user defined depth interval from an ODF file.
Yes Yes ODF Update File OUF Files_ OUF Concept Small and sequential update files, which only contain updated information since the last file save.
Ordinarily sent as daily updates from the well site to the operation offices.
Yes GEO Draft Output Database File GDF
This is a file format equivalent to the ODF, but created by the GEO Draft application.
These files may be opened by applications of the GEO Software Suite, to allow full data sharing with users of the GEO Draft application.
No Yes GEO Draft View File GDV
This is a file format equivalent to the VEW, but created by the GEO Draft application.
These files may be opened by applications of the GEO Software Suite, to allow full data sharing with users of the GEO Draft application.
Yes GEO Graph Database file GGD
This is the file type created by the GEO Graph application.
This file can be opened and edited using GEO Graph but the files can be added to ODF or ODT files for display purposes.
Yes Yes GEO Graph Template file GGT
This is the template version of the GGD file.
This file can be opened and edited using GEO Graph and be used like an GGD, but saves no data or data related features.
CGM is standard feature in GEO, while OUF is a standard feature only in GEO and GEO Lite.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Working_with_Files\ODF_Interval_Files_(OIF).htm =====

ODF Interval Files ( OIF ) ODF Interval Files ( OIF ) ODF Interval Files ( OIF )
If an ODF file, has a data range of 0-10000ft, but only a specific depth range, 7000-8000ft is of interest, sending an ODF with the remaining 9000ft of data is unnecessary and inefficient.
Instead, an OIF file containing the 7000-8000ft of data can be saved, creating a much smaller file.
To save an OIF File Display the depth range required.
On the Depth tab, enter the From and To index range i. e. 7000-8000.
On the GEO menu, select Save Displayed Depth or Time interval As ( OIF )… Enter a File name and select Save.

• Enter a File name and select Save .

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Working_with_Files\ODF_Template_File_(ODT).htm =====

ODF Template File ( ODT ) ODF Template File ( ODT ) ODF Template File ( ODT )
A template ( ODT ) can be created from fresh or from an existing ODF file.
This means once a preferred format has been created it can be saved as a template and utilized thereafter.
Unlike a View file (a file with VEW extension), which only saves the track layout, the template function saves all the ODF constituents in a template format.
This ensures that preferred components, such as library files (i. e. lithology, headers with included location maps, symbols, modifiers) are incorporated into the template.
Any plot objects in the ODF will also be incorporated into the template saved.
Once an ODT file has been created, it may be distributed to other users.
The ODT file is a powerful tool when a final log format has been approved.
The ODT file will always contain library information (headers, lithology, modifiers, structures, and symbols), view file contents (track layout information, depth and screen units, scale and pen information (optional)) and ini file settings (curve defaults, computed curves and table definitions).
GEONet Template Customization Service Create your own Template You can create an ODT from an ODF using a wizard, which allows users to include or omit further plot elements from an existing ODF.
This option allows you to see information within the ODT organized in a tree structure.
It will warn you if some components of the ODT are not functioning correctly or have settings that are deemed not best practice.
When creating a template you can consult the document information tree to see what warnings appear, that would otherwise be not obvious.
You can therefore attempt to rectify them.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Working_with_Files\ODF_Update_File_(OUF).htm =====

ODF Update File ( OUF ) ODF Update File ( OUF ) ODF Update File ( OUF )
The ODF Update File or OUF, enables you to send daily updates with a high level of security, very cost effectively.
The prime purposes are adding security when e-mailing files (the OUF files must be loaded sequentially) and reducing the size, and therefore cost, of e-mailing daily updates over expensive satellite links.
The OUF file only carries ‘Update’ information; as a result the size of the files is reduced substantially.
While an ODF is being created at the wellsite, the size and complexity of the file increases throughout the duration of the well, as progressively more data is added to it.
The security of mailing the file becomes increasingly important, as do the actual costs involved.
In the scenario where a wellsite user e-mails files to an operations base, the sending of the entire ODF on a daily basis can become inefficient.
This is especially true when the recipient of the ODF is only concerned with the updates.
In the OUF model, the Wellsite user creates and maintains a Parent ODF.
From this is saved sequential OUF files.
These files are then mailed to the operations base and loaded to build an identical Child ODF.
The OUF files must be loaded in the correct sequence to successfully build the Child ODF.
The scenario below attempts to show the best practice on how this OUF model may be conducted.
At the Wellsite The first time the ODF is saved, you simply select Save
As from the GEO menu and supply a file name as normal.
When the first transfer of data from the wellsite to operations base is required, you would simply select Save OUF Updates from the GEO menu (or Send OUF Update Via Mail if you are going to send the file directly through an e-mail facility already present and set up in your PC – requires internet connection).
GEO takes the file name supplied and creates the first OUF file.
You would then e-mail, disk-fax or modem transfer the ‘WellX- 001.
ouf ’ to the operations base, instead of the WellX. odf.
Because of its in-built compressibility, the resultant OUF file will always be smaller than the Parent ODF, although for the very first transmission, there probably will not be such a marked difference in file sizes as is noticeable with the subsequent OUF s. Between transfers, the wellsite user can of course keep the Parent ODF up-to-date and saved on the local drive by using the normal Save procedure from the GEO menu.
For the next transfer, you would again select Save OUF Updates or Send OUF Update Via Mail.
GEO will then save this update as an OUF, called WellX-002.
ouf will simultaneously save the WellX. odf to the same point.
If you select Save As instead of Save OUF Updates it would result in a GEO warning message (840) advising you that saving the ODF to another name would break the connection between this ODF and all subsequent OUF s’.
Hence, say if the ODF was saved under a different name e. g. WellZ. odf.
The next time you go to Save OUF Updates the OUF would revert to WellZ- 001.
ouf because of the name change.
All the information loaded would then be encapsulated in this new OUF under the newly named ODF.
At the Operations Base You have two options for loading the OUF file.
Double-clicking on the OUF e-mail attachment.
This would launch GEO and load the OUF file automatically.
Detaching the e-mail attachment and selecting Load OUF Updates from the GEO menu After loading the 001.
ouf, the file must be saved as an ODF.
You can give a file name as appropriate.
The ODF created is often called the ‘Child’ ODF.
Each time an OUF is received and loaded, the ODF is saved prior to loading subsequent OUF s.
This ensures the child ODF is at the correct stage to load the next OUF in sequence.
The OUF s must be loaded in sequence.
If the wellsite user accidentally sends 004.
ouf without previously sending 003.
ouf the operations base user cannot load the file.
This is an important security element of the OUF file.
Please note, that OUF files may be opened and viewed within the full viewer application, GEO View.
OUF files cannot be opened directly using the free viewer, GEO e-View.
Files must first be consolidated within an ODF file (using GEO or GEO View).
After the ODF has been e-View enabled (using GEO ), it may only then be freely shared with users of the GEO e-View application.
What happens if the OUF connection is broken?
Any amendments made in the PARENT ODF, and the OUF subsequently created, will over-ride changes made in the Child ODF.
The Replication Information dialog box serves to advise the operations base user, if an amendment made in the Child ODF, has also been changed in the OUF they are loading.
This is the only scenario where a Replication Information dialog box is invoked detailing a Replication Conflict.
Example: The operations base user loads an OUF.
They then move a casing shoe symbol from 4000ft to 4500ft, and save the child ODF.
The next OUF received includes the same casing shoe having been moved in the PARENT ODF from 4000ft to 4250ft.
When the operations base user loads this OUF they will first see a Replication Information dialog box.
This advises the operations base user that a change made to the child ODF has also been changed in the parent ODF.
Exiting the dialog box will over-write the change made by the operations user in the child ODF.
After loading this OUF the casing shoe will be moved to 4250ft.
GEO takes the OUF to be loaded and checks the contents of this OUF against the contents of the child ODF.
In the above example, the Replication Information dialog box would not have been produced if the symbol had not been moved in the PARENT ODF.
The child ODF can be altered any number of times without invoking the ‘Replication Conflict’, as long as an alteration using the same log object has not been implemented in the parent ODF.
Further Example: A sandstone block has two pyritic modifiers at 3000ft. GEO assigns these modifiers their own unique id numbers (e. g. 20 & 21).
The child ODF is altered, by shifting modifier 20 to 2995ft and then saved.
The PARENT ODF is altered, by shifting modifier 21 to 3005ft.
The next sequential OUF is then saved.
When this OUF is loaded into the child ODF, a Replication Information dialog box will not open.
If however, in a later OUF, modifier 20 is shifted from 3000ft to 3005ft, upon loading this OUF a Replication Information dialog box is opened.
This is because the OUF records the shift from 3000ft to 3005ft in the parent ODF.
When scanning the child ODF, GEO by default, assumes the modifier to be positioned at 3000ft but upon loading the OUF scans and records the same modifier (20), positioned at 2995ft.
This ‘deviation’ invokes the Replication Information dialog box.

• Double-clicking on the OUF e-mail attachment. This would launch GEO and load the OUF file automatically.
• Detaching the e-mail attachment and selecting Load OUF Updates from the GEO menu

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Working_with_Files\Output_Database_File_(ODF).htm =====

Output Database File ( ODF ) Output Database File ( ODF )
Output Database File ( ODF )
The Output Database File or ODF is the compact database file created by GEO.
It contains all information needed for rapid recall of all data relating to a particular well, either for further editing/update or for recreating the log.
The main components of an ODF are: Any loaded curve data and information about their source.
Layout related information, such as tracks, and the log scale Information about geological interpretation data, such as lithology, symbol and modifiers.
Information that you input, such as remarks, texts, tables and headers / trailers.
All libraries and fonts of the system in which the ODF was first created.
Embedded objects, such as documents, spreadsheets, maps, diagrams, photographs, etc. Links to related external documents, such as reports, spreadsheets, photographs, other ODF s, etc. ODF files may be shared with other members of the team (or with well partners) who require read-only access to the log and embedded curve data, using GEO View, or the free viewer, GEO e-View.
For added security, an ODF must first be made e-View enabled before it can be opened by GEO e-View.
The bottom status bar will state if the open ODF is e-View enabled or disabled.
If disabled, right click on it and select e-View enabled.
Both GEO View and GEO e-View can operate as ‘plug-in’ controls to the Internet Explorer web browser, so effectively allowing ODF files to be opened (normally by clicking a hyperlink to the ODF on an intranet web-page) within this standard browser.
(If you are interested in setting-up a corporate intranet for securely-sharing your well data, please contact your local office of Geologix Limited.
We shall be pleased to discuss your requirements and to offer our expertise within a range of service solutions).

• Any loaded curve data and information about their source.
• Layout related information, such as tracks, and the log scale
• Information about geological interpretation data, such as lithology, symbol and modifiers.
• Information that you input, such as remarks, texts, tables and headers / trailers.
• All libraries and fonts of the system in which the ODF was first created.
• Embedded objects, such as documents, spreadsheets, maps, diagrams, photographs, etc.
• Links to related external documents, such as reports, spreadsheets, photographs, other ODFs, etc.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\introduction\Working_with_Files\Save_an_ODF.htm =====

Save an ODF Save an ODF When an ODF file is saved in GEO, all curve data along with any other data such as lithology, modifiers, symbols, and texts will be saved.
In addition, all other information that is required to reproduce the log as it was at the time of saving (such as track layout, curve presentation attributes, zoom factors, header/trailer layout and mnemonics) is also saved.
Save a new ODF On the GEO menu, select Save As.
In Save in, browse to the location where you wish to save the ODF.
This can be up to 255 characters long, including the space and path names.
In Save as type, select Geo Documents (*. ODF ).
Save an existing ODF On the GEO menu, select Save.
Or, Select the Save button on the quick access toolbar.
Each time an ODF is modified, an Asterix (*) will appear against the ODF name on the title bar.
This indicates that the ODF needs to be saved to retain the changes made since the last save.

• On the GEO menu, select Save As .
• In Save in , browse to the location where you wish to save the ODF.
• Type a File name . This can be up to 255 characters long, including the space and path names.
• In Save as type , select Geo Documents (*.ODF) .
• Select Save .
