===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\visualization\Curve_Display\Present_Curve_in_Tadpole_Format.htm =====

Present Curve in Tadpole Format Present Curve in Tadpole Format A tadpole plot is used to present four data sets in graphical format.
The four data sets are: Dip/Deviation : these values must fall between 0 and 90 degrees Azimuth : these values must fall between 0 and 360 degrees Quality : this data is optional and n ormally represented by a % figure Dip Type : this data is optional.
It consists of integers which represent specific dip types The Dip/Deviation is represented by the position of the tadpole body on the track where the track edges reflect the two extremes of dip; 0 and 90 degrees.
The Azimuth is depicted by the orientation of the tadpole ‘tail’.
The Quality is reflected by the ‘fill’ of the tadpole body.
Four quality thresholds can be defined.
The Dip Type can be reflected either by the tadpole color or the 'Dip Name' which displays in the track legend.
Present tadpoles on the plot Please ensure that appropriate tadpole curve data has been loaded into the ODF.
Ensure that the curve data has been configured as ' Tadpole Data ' - on the Curve tab, select Curve Settings, the Curve Settings sidebar will open.
Select the tadpole data from the Curve list, then Close the list.
O pen the Data tab and expand the Display node.
T he Use Data for Tadpole Presentation should be ticked.
On the Workflows tab, select Tadpole Definitions.
The Tadpole Definitions will open.
For a new tadpole definition, select an unused number from the Select a Definition.
Enter a name for this tadpole definition in the Definition Name box.
Tick both the In Use and Display on Plot check boxes in order to display this tadpole definition on your log.
Select appropriate curves for the Dip/Deviation, Azimuth, Quality and Dip Type by clicking on the down arrow to the right of their corresponding boxes and choosing from the tadpole data available.
If referencing a Dip Type curve, please define each dip type by filling in the appropriate fields in the panel to the right of the Dip Type box.
To add more rows to the panel, use the keyboard down arrow.
If you wish to display tadpoles with undefined dip types, please ensure that you tick the Display Tadpoles on Plot with Undefined Dip Types check box.
Select the track that you wish to display the tadpoles on in the Track for plotting Tadpole Data box and the dip/deviation data scale at the Left edge and Right edge boxes.
Define the Quality threshold by entering an appropriate value for each fill type in the corresponding boxes.
Adjust the tadpole Circle Diameter and its Tail length in the Tadpole Symbol Parameters section.

• Dip/Deviation : these values must fall between 0 and 90 degrees
• Azimuth : these values must fall between 0 and 360 degrees
• Quality : this data is optional and n ormally represented by a % figure
• Dip Type : this data is optional. It consists of integers which represent specific dip types
• Please ensure that appropriate tadpole curve data has been loaded into the ODF .

T he Use Data for Tadpole Presentation should be ticked.

Save the Curve Display Settings (Defaults) Save the Curve Display Settings (Defaults) Save the Curve Display Settings (Defaults)
The display settings for each curve, such as curve mnemonic, scale, pen type, pen color, name and measurement units, auto populate capabilities etc., can be saved as defaults for future usage.
On the Curves tab, select Curve Settings.
The Curve Settings sidebar will open.
Select the Curve, then Close the list.
Ensure its display properties are as required.
Do this for each curve you wish to save the default display settings for.
The defaults will then be stored within the geocurve.
ini file, which usually resides in the GEO library directory.
ini file can be loaded into other ODF’s and the saved defaults applied to the curves within.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\visualization\Curve_Shading,_Splicing_and_Depth_Shifting\Apply_Curve_Shading.htm =====

Apply Curve Shading Apply Curve Shading Shade the region between two curves, between a track edge and a curve or between a fixed value and a curve, with a user-selected color, fill or lithology pattern.
This is useful in highlighting curve features such as density-neutron crossovers, invasion profiles, hole washouts or clean sand cut offs.
On the Curve s tab, select Curve Shading.
The Cur ve Shading Information dialog box will open.
From Curve Shading, select an unused curve number.
Up to 250 shadings can be applied in one ODF.
Select Display Curve Shade to display the shading on the plot.
Select the Track where the curve shading will apply.
Tick Cover track Grids to shade over the plot grid.
Un -tick to display grids over the shading.
In Shade From, specify the starting point of the shading by selecting a curve, fixed value or corresponding track edge.
In To, specify the end shading point by selecting a curve, fixed value or corresponding track edge.
If <fixed curve value> is selected either as start or end shading point, the value needs to be specified in Fixed Curve Value.
Click Append to define a shading interval and its pattern through the Zone Attributes grid.
This grid is used to select the shading’s fill type, color, and depth range over which the shade will occur.
Enter the shading depth interval in the From Depth and To Depth columns.
To select the entire curve interval, leave From Depth as 0 and To Depth as 99999.
This allows the curve shading to extend automatically, for instance, when subsequent curves are appended to those existing at the time of setting-up that curve shade.
Solid single color for the entire shading.
Double-click the Left Color column.
The Color dialog box will open.
Select or mix your shading color.
RGB -> RGB : Color degradation from left to the right.
Double click the Left Color followed by the Right Color columns, so you can select different colors between left and right edge of shading.
Hue Fill : Change in Hue from left to right.
Saturation Fill : Saturation degradation/intensity increase.
Luminosity Fill : Luminosity coloration changes (greyscale).
None : No shading RGB > RGB (vertical) : Color gradation vertically based on zone attributes.
Each row in zone attributes represents a shade from one color to the next, based on the discriminating curve.
Select Update to apply the changes.
Curve Shade based on discriminating Curve The shading can be based on particular curve values, either by defining shading zones based on those curve values, or by referencing a curve composed of RGB data.
From Shade based on discriminating curve, select the corresponding curve.
Tick Data the contains RGB Values if your curve consists of RGB values.
Select Data Value Ranges defined below if you with to define shading zones.
If you select < Curve from Mnemonic >
the radio buttons will not enable and the Data Value Ranges defined below will be selected by default.
A new drop list will appear from with you can select the Mnemonic.
The shading interval in the Zone Attributes grid will change to From Value and To Value (instead of From Depth and To Depth).
To delete shading from the plot, select the Curve Shading and clear Display Curve Shade on Layout, then Update.
Although all names remain on this dialog box for later re-selection, the shading is removed from the plot.
To totally remove the settings click Reset.

Apply Lithologies as Curve Shading Apply Lithologies as Curve Shading Lithologies can be applied as curve shading in two ways.
Lithology shading through a cut off or fixed value.
Lithology shading based on the value of curve.
Apply Lithology Shading Through a Cut Off or Fixed Value Example: Shade GR curve with sandstone pattern if its value is less than 40 API.
On the Curves tab, select Curve Shading.
The Curve Shading Information dialog box will open.
From Curve Shading, select an unused curve number.
Select Display Curve Shade to display the shading on the plot.
Enter a curve shading Name.
Select the Track where the GR curve displays.
In Shade from select GR.
In To select <fixed curve value>.
In Fixed Curve enter 40.
In the Zone Attributes grid Type column, select Pattern.
In the Pattern column, select Sandstone.
vob must be present in your ODF file as a lithology.
Select the shading depth interval by entering appropriate depth interval in From Depth and To Depth column at Zone Attributes.
Apply lithology shading based on the curve values Example: Shade GR curve with sandstone if GR value is less than 40 API, with claystone if GR value between 40 and 80 API and with shale if GR value is greater than 80 API.
On the Curves tab, select Curve Shading.

From Curve Shading, select an unused curve number.

Enter a curve shading Name.

In To select <right edge of track>.
In Shade based on value of discriminating curve select GR (instead of None).
In Zone Attributes grid, leave the From Value as it is (which by default is the minimum value of the GR curve) and enter 40 in To Value.
In the Type column, select Pattern.
In the Pattern column, select Sandstone.
In the second row of Zone Attributes grid, enter 40 in the From Value and enter 80 in To Value column.
Define the Type column as Pattern.
In the Pattern column, select Claystone.
In the third row of Zone Attributes grid, enter 80 in the From Value and leave the maximum GR value in To Value column.
The curve shading information entered in Zone Attributes can be copied, by clicking Copy.
You can then Paste it into a different ODF.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\visualization\Curve_Shading,_Splicing_and_Depth_Shifting\Curve_Depth_Shifting.htm =====

Curve Depth Shifting Curve Depth Shifting The depth of curves can be shifted to shallower or deeper depths using the depth shifts feature.
To access this, on the Depths tab, select Curves and Global Depth Shifts.
The Depth Shift Specifications dialog box will open.
From here you can perform the following actions.
Global Depth Shift All Curves by a particular amount.
In the Depth Shift Specifications dialog box, enter the Shift value, that you wish to move all the curves by.
Check Apply Global Shift t o Curves, then Apply.
It is not possible to shift a section of curve when performing a global depth shift.
Only the whole curve can be shifted.
Depth Shift Individual Curves Shift the depths of individual curves.
This is also knows as rubber banding.
In Depth Shift Specifications, select the individual curve you wish to shift from Curve Related Depth Shift.
Click Create Curve Depth Shift – two depth shift rows will appear in the grid The Depth column, states the first (start) depth and second (end) depth of the selected curve.
The values can be changed by typing in the cell.
The Shift column, states the amount the depth point has been shifted by.
To shift the curve, enter the amount you wish to shift the first depth and second depth by, in their corresponding Shift cell.
Add more depth points to shift by selecting Insert Row.
To delete inserted rows, select them and click Delete Row.
Apply Same Rubber Banding Shifts To Other Curves You can copy the depth shift pattern specified for an individual curve, to another curve.
In Depth Shift Specifications, select the curve with the shift pattern you wish to copy in Curve Related Depth Shift.
Click Copy Curve Depth Shift.
Select the curve you wish to apply the shift pattern to in the Curve Related Depth Shift drop list.
Click Paste from Curve x (the x will be the number of the curve), then Exit.
Remove the Depth Shift In Depth Shift Specifications, select the curve you wish to remove the depth shift for in the Curve Related Depth Shift drop list.
Select Remove Curve Depth Shift.
All Depth Shifts for the curve will be deleted and the original (unshifted) depths restored.
View Depth Shift Details There is an additional dialog box accessed via the Depth Shift Specifications where you can view each shift depth point and the data value associated with it.
This is called the Curve Depth Details.
In this dialog box you can also remove the shift and revert to the original data, or you can preserve the new shifted data with no evidence of a shift.
In Depth Shift Specifications, select Curve Depth Details.
The Curve Depth Details dialog box will open.
Select a Curve you wish to analyse.
The Current Depth, Computed Depth and Value or each data point in the curve will be listed.
To remove the depth shift, select Revert t o Original Dept hs, then Remove.
GEO Message:816 will appear - click Yes.
To make the shifted depths the 'true' data points of the curve (there will be no evidence this curve was depth shifted), select Preserve Current Depths, then Remove.
GEO Message:826 will appear - click
Click Exit to return to the Depth Shift Specification s.
The curve selection will need to be refreshed to reflect any changes made in the the Curve Depth Details.

• Check Apply Global Shift t o Curves , then Apply . Note . It is not possible to shift a section of curve when performing a global depth shift. Only the whole curve can be shifted.
• In Depth Shift Specifications , select the individual curve you wish to shift from Curve Related Depth Shift .

• Add more depth points to shift by selecting Insert Row .

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\visualization\Curve_Shading,_Splicing_and_Depth_Shifting\Shade_Wrapped_Curve.htm =====

Shade Wrapped Curves Shade Wrapped Curves Shade between the wrapped (or out-of scale value) curves and the left or right track edge.
For example, an ROP curve that has data range between 0 to 380 ft/min needs to be displayed with left and right edge scale at 0 to 300 ft/min.
To indicate a fast drilling region, a red curve shading needs to be applied between left track edge and any ROP curve whose value is greater than 300 ft/min. Ensure that the ROP curve has been wrapped right at least once, so the out-of-scale curve will be displayed on the track.
On the Curves tab, select Curve Shading.
The Curve Shading Information dialog box will open.
From Curve Shading, select an unused number.
Tick Display Curve Shade on Layout.
Enter a curve shading Name.
Select the Track where the ROP curve displays.
In Shade From, select <left edge of track>.
In To, select the wrapped ROP curve and tick Wrapped below.
Click Append and select the shading color as Red.
Only the wrapped ROP (i. e. its value exceeding 300 ft/min) will then be shaded red.

• On the Curves tab, select Curve Shading . The Curve Shading Information dialog box will open.
• From Curve Shading , select an unused number.
• Tick Display Curve Shade on Layout .
• Enter a curve shading Name .
• Select the Track where the ROP curve displays.
• In Shade From , select <left edge of track> .
• In To , select the wrapped ROP curve and tick Wrapped below.
• Click Append and select the shading color as Red .
• Select Update .

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\visualization\Curve_Shading,_Splicing_and_Depth_Shifting\Splice.htm =====

Splice Curves Splice Curves Take portions of different curves and splice them together to form a new curve.
The selected source curve is spliced onto the destination curve over the specified depth interval.
In general, the splicing operation is appropriate only for wireline curves.
This is because each wireline curve has its own first and last reading and curves need to be spliced to eliminate or minimize data falling outside these points.
The File ID of a spliced curve is [Spliced], indicating that the data is not original.
You are only able to splice curves into [Unused] or [Spliced] destinations so that the original data is left intact in case a spliced curve needs to be recreated with different splice points.
Mudlog data, on the other hand, should be appended rather than spliced as the data provided on a daily basis from the mudloggers constitute part of a continuous data-set.
However, sometimes, to satisfy the requirement of presenting ROP with different scales over different zones, the one ROP curve may be split up into the different zones using the splice function.
On the Curves tab, select Splice.
The Curve Splicing dialog box will open.
Select a curve from Source Curve.
The depth range of the curve will be displayed at the side.
In Select range to copy enter the start and end depth respectively.
The depth range entered must be the same or a subset of the source curve depth range.
Select a curve from Destination Curve on to which the source curve will be spliced.
Initially, the destination curve must be an [Unused] one.
The curve in Destination Curve will then bear the same mnemonic as the source curve and have a File ID of [Spliced].
Another Source Curve can be selected and a new data set can be spliced, by leaving the Destination Curve the same as what you have in step 5.
Click Splice to then splice two different curves from the Source Curve into one curve (as specified in the Destination Curve ).
If the source curve is being copied onto an existing curve, and there is an overlap between the source and destination curves, a dialog box will be presented.
Yes: overwrites the overlapping section of the destination curve with source curve values.
No: retains the destination curve values over the section of the overlap.
The above process may be repeated on the same destination curve with other source curves.
Select Index Converter to calculate the different depth values (in MD, TVD, TVD SS, TWT and VSEC ) for a specific depth without exiting the dialog box.

• On the Curves tab, select Splice . The Curve Splicing dialog box will open.
• Select a curve from Source Curve . The depth range of the curve will be displayed at the side.
• In Select range to copy enter the start and end depth respectively. The depth range entered must be the same or a subset of the source curve depth range.
• Select a curve from Destination Curve on to which the source curve will be spliced. Initially, the destination curve must be an [Unused] one.
• Click Splice . The curve in Destination Curve will then bear the same mnemonic as the source curve and have a File ID of [Spliced] .
• Another Source Curve can be selected and a new data set can be spliced, by leaving the Destination Curve the same as what you have in step 5.
• Click Splice to then splice two different curves from the Source Curve into one curve (as specified in the Destination Curve ).
• If the source curve is being copied onto an existing curve, and there is an overlap between the source and destination curves, a dialog box will be presented. Yes: overwrites the overlapping section of the destination curve with source curve values. No: retains the destination curve values over the section of the overlap. Cancel: aborts the operation.
• Yes: overwrites the overlapping section of the destination curve with source curve values.
• No: retains the destination curve values over the section of the overlap.
• Cancel: aborts the operation.
• The above process may be repeated on the same destination curve with other source curves.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\visualization\Curve_Shading_and_Splicing\Apply_Curve_Shading.htm =====

Apply Curve Shading Apply Curve Shading Shade the region between two curves, between a track edge and a curve or between a fixed value and a curve, with a user-selected color, fill or lithology pattern.
This is useful in highlighting curve features such as density-neutron crossovers, invasion profiles, hole washouts or clean sand cut offs.
On the Curve s tab, select Curve Shading.
The Cur ve Shading Information dialog box will open.
From Curve Shading, select an unused curve number.
Up to 250 shadings can be applied in one ODF.
Select Display Curve Shade to display the shading on the plot.
Select the Track where the curve shading will apply.
Tick Cover track Grids to shade over the plot grid.
Un -tick to display grids over the shading.
In Shade From, specify the starting point of the shading by selecting a curve, fixed value or corresponding track edge.
In To, specify the end shading point by selecting a curve, fixed value or corresponding track edge.
If <fixed curve value> is selected either as start or end shading point, the value needs to be specified in Fixed Curve Value.
Click Append to define a shading interval and its pattern through the Zone Attributes grid.
This grid is used to select the shading’s fill type, color, and depth range over which the shade will occur.
Enter the shading depth interval in the From Depth and To Depth columns.
To select the entire curve interval, leave From Depth as 0 and To Depth as 99999.
This allows the curve shading to extend automatically, for instance, when subsequent curves are appended to those existing at the time of setting-up that curve shade.
Solid single color for the entire shading.
Double-click the Left Color column.
The Color dialog box will open.
Select or mix your shading color.
RGB -> RGB : Color degradation from left to the right.
Double click the Left Color followed by the Right Color columns, so you can select different colors between left and right edge of shading.
Hue Fill : Change in Hue from left to right.
Saturation Fill : Saturation degradation/intensity increase.
Luminosity Fill : Luminosity coloration changes (greyscale).
None : No shading RGB > RGB (vertical) : Color gradation vertically based on zone attributes.
Each row in zone attributes represents a shade from one color to the next, based on the discriminating curve.
Select Update to apply the changes.
Curve Shade based on discriminating Curve The shading can be based on particular curve values, either by defining shading zones based on those curve values, or by referencing a curve composed of RGB data.
From Shade based on discriminating curve, select the corresponding curve.
Tick Data the contains RGB Values if your curve consists of RGB values.
Select Data Value Ranges defined below if you with to define shading zones.
If you select < Curve from Mnemonic >
the radio buttons will not enable and the Data Value Ranges defined below will be selected by default.
A new drop list will appear from with you can select the Mnemonic.
The shading interval in the Zone Attributes grid will change to From Value and To Value (instead of From Depth and To Depth).
To delete shading from the plot, select the Curve Shading and clear Display Curve Shade on Layout, then Update.
Although all names remain on this dialog box for later re-selection, the shading is removed from the plot.
To totally remove the settings click Reset.

Apply Lithologies as Curve Shading Apply Lithologies as Curve Shading Lithologies can be applied as curve shading in two ways.
Lithology shading through a cut off or fixed value.
Lithology shading based on the value of curve.
Apply Lithology Shading Through a Cut Off or Fixed Value Example: Shade GR curve with sandstone pattern if its value is less than 40 API.
On the Curves tab, select Curve Shading.
The Curve Shading Information dialog box will open.
From Curve Shading, select an unused curve number.
Select Display Curve Shade to display the shading on the plot.
Enter a curve shading Name.
Select the Track where the GR curve displays.
In Shade from select GR.
In To select <fixed curve value>.
In Fixed Curve enter 40.
In the Zone Attributes grid Type column, select Pattern.
In the Pattern column, select Sandstone.
vob must be present in your ODF file as a lithology.
Select the shading depth interval by entering appropriate depth interval in From Depth and To Depth column at Zone Attributes.
Apply lithology shading based on the curve values Example: Shade GR curve with sandstone if GR value is less than 40 API, with claystone if GR value between 40 and 80 API and with shale if GR value is greater than 80 API.
On the Curves tab, select Curve Shading.
The Curve Shading Information dialog box will open.
From Curve Shading, select an unused curve number.

In Zone Attributes grid, leave the From Value as it is (which by default is the minimum value of the GR curve) and enter 40 in To Value.
In the Type column, select Pattern.
In the Pattern column, select Sandstone.
In the second row of Zone Attributes grid, enter 40 in the From Value and enter 80 in To Value column.
Define the Type column as Pattern.
In the Pattern column, select Claystone.
In the third row of Zone Attributes grid, enter 80 in the From Value and leave the maximum GR value in To Value column.
The curve shading information entered in Zone Attributes can be copied, by clicking Copy.
You can then Paste it into a different ODF.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\visualization\Curve_Shading_and_Splicing\Shade_Wrapped_Curve.htm =====

Shade Wrapped Curves Shade Wrapped Curves Shade between the wrapped (or out-of scale value) curves and the left or right track edge.
For example, an ROP curve that has data range between 0 to 380 ft/min needs to be displayed with left and right edge scale at 0 to 300 ft/min.
To indicate a fast drilling region, a red curve shading needs to be applied between left track edge and any ROP curve whose value is greater than 300 ft/min. Ensure that the ROP curve has been wrapped right at least once, so the out-of-scale curve will be displayed on the track.
On the Curves tab, select Curve Shading.
The Curve Shading Information dialog box will open.
From Curve Shading, select an unused number.
Tick Display Curve Shade on Layout.
Enter a curve shading Name.
Select the Track where the ROP curve displays.
In Shade From, select <left edge of track>.
In To, select the wrapped ROP curve and tick Wrapped below.
Click Append and select the shading color as Red.
Only the wrapped ROP (i. e. its value exceeding 300 ft/min) will then be shaded red.

• On the Curves tab, select Curve Shading . The Curve Shading Information dialog box will open.
• From Curve Shading , select an unused number.
• Tick Display Curve Shade on Layout .
• Enter a curve shading Name .
• Select the Track where the ROP curve displays.
• In Shade From , select <left edge of track> .
• In To , select the wrapped ROP curve and tick Wrapped below.
• Click Append and select the shading color as Red .
• Select Update .

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\visualization\Curve_Shading_and_Splicing\Splice.htm =====

Splice Curves Splice Curves Take portions of different curves and splice them together to form a new curve.
The selected source curve is spliced onto the destination curve over the specified depth interval.
In general, the splicing operation is appropriate only for wireline curves.
This is because each wireline curve has its own first and last reading and curves need to be spliced to eliminate or minimize data falling outside these points.
The File ID of a spliced curve is [Spliced], indicating that the data is not original.
You are only able to splice curves into [Unused] or [Spliced] destinations so that the original data is left intact in case a spliced curve needs to be recreated with different splice points.
Mudlog data, on the other hand, should be appended rather than spliced as the data provided on a daily basis from the mudloggers constitute part of a continuous data-set.
However, sometimes, to satisfy the requirement of presenting ROP with different scales over different zones, the one ROP curve may be split up into the different zones using the splice function.
On the Curves tab, select Splice.
The Curve Splicing dialog box will open.
Select a curve from Source Curve.
The depth range of the curve will be displayed at the side.
In Select range to copy enter the start and end depth respectively.
The depth range entered must be the same or a subset of the source curve depth range.
Select a curve from Destination Curve on to which the source curve will be spliced.
Initially, the destination curve must be an [Unused] one.
The curve in Destination Curve will then bear the same mnemonic as the source curve and have a File ID of [Spliced].
Another Source Curve can be selected and a new data set can be spliced, by leaving the Destination Curve the same as what you have in step 5.
Click Splice to then splice two different curves from the Source Curve into one curve (as specified in the Destination Curve ).
If the source curve is being copied onto an existing curve, and there is an overlap between the source and destination curves, a dialog box will be presented.
Yes: overwrites the overlapping section of the destination curve with source curve values.
No: retains the destination curve values over the section of the overlap.
The above process may be repeated on the same destination curve with other source curves.
Select Index Converter to calculate the different depth values (in MD, TVD, TVD SS, TWT and VSEC ) for a specific depth without exiting the dialog box.

• On the Curves tab, select Splice . The Curve Splicing dialog box will open.
• Select a curve from Source Curve . The depth range of the curve will be displayed at the side.
• In Select range to copy enter the start and end depth respectively. The depth range entered must be the same or a subset of the source curve depth range.
• Select a curve from Destination Curve on to which the source curve will be spliced. Initially, the destination curve must be an [Unused] one.
• Click Splice . The curve in Destination Curve will then bear the same mnemonic as the source curve and have a File ID of [Spliced] .
• Another Source Curve can be selected and a new data set can be spliced, by leaving the Destination Curve the same as what you have in step 5.
• Click Splice to then splice two different curves from the Source Curve into one curve (as specified in the Destination Curve ).
• If the source curve is being copied onto an existing curve, and there is an overlap between the source and destination curves, a dialog box will be presented. Yes: overwrites the overlapping section of the destination curve with source curve values. No: retains the destination curve values over the section of the overlap. Cancel: aborts the operation.
• Yes: overwrites the overlapping section of the destination curve with source curve values.
• No: retains the destination curve values over the section of the overlap.
• Cancel: aborts the operation.
• The above process may be repeated on the same destination curve with other source curves.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\visualization\GEOGraph\GEOGraph_Introduction.htm =====

GEO Graph Introduction GEO Graph Introduction GEO Graph is an integrated application which allows you to create X-Y and Z plots from curve data or table data from within GEO.
This Graphs can then be displayed in the header or trailer.
Uses can range from well trajectory plots through to pressure plots.
Once the data is plotted, calculations of best-fit lines and line intersect can be achieved.
This accompanied by full integration with GEO serves as a useful graphics tool.
Benefits of using GEO Graph The focus throughout the GEO software Suite is to promote a minimal ‘time and effort’ logic.
The GEO / GEO Graph integration is no different as once you have created your Graph and placed it in a header or trailer it becomes completely dynamic.
Meaning if the data your graph is based on is changed or amended your GEO Graph document will automatically update.
This can be as a result of editing or importing Curve or Table data.
This also means if your GEO Graph document is set up in a blank ODT for example, when you load in applicable data, the GEO Graph document will automatically populate with the data.
You can invoke GEO Graph within a GEO document by double-clicking on the GEO Graph document displayed in the header or trailer area.
Learn how to a dd a graph (ggd file) to your ODF or ODT.
As part of the installation routine you will probably have installed a suite of example files and templates that have some example graphs already set up for you.
Please feel free to experiment with these files and see how GEO Graph could benefit your well log.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\visualization\Lines\Add_L.htm =====

Add Line ↵ ↵ Add Line Draw a line on the plot.
On the Home tab, select Line.
The cursor will display the text ST. LINE to indicate that the mouse may be used to define the starting position of a line.
Place the mouse at the point where the line should start and click.
The cursor text will change to EN. Line.
Place the mouse at the point where the line should end and click.
The Line Definition dialog box will open.
Select the line Type and Color.
Re-position the line by entering the depth and X-position of the start and end line, in Start and End point attributes.
You can also change the anchor for the start and end of line, by selecting from the Anchor box.
The X-position depends on the anchor point.
You need to enter to which track the anchor is to be made, if you select either Left or Right edge of track in the Anchor section.
To add an arrow to the line, select from the Arrow Styles.
Click New to enter free format text that will be associated/related to the line.
The Free Format Text Entry sidebar will open.
Click to learn how to add free format text.
Click OK to draw the line on the log.
During line copy-paste process, only a horizontal line can be pasted in the plot with the Start point independent from the mouse pointer position.
If a tilted (incline) line is copied, it will be pasted with the Start point at the mouse pointer position (when you do a right click over the plot before clicking Paste ).
If the <Shift> key is depressed before the end point is defined, a vertical line will be drawn from the starting point to the depth where the end point is clicked.
If the <Ctrl> key is depressed before the end point is defined, a diagonal line will be drawn from the starting point to the end point.
Please note that this type of line can only be created with custom or solid lines.
To terminate the line definition mode, prior to defining the end point, press the <Esc> key.

• On the Home tab, select Line . The cursor will display the text ST.LINE to indicate that the mouse may be used to define the starting position of a line.
• Place the mouse at the point where the line should start and click. The cursor text will change to EN.Line .
• Place the mouse at the point where the line should end and click. The Line Definition dialog box will open.
• Select the line Type and Color .
• Re-position the line by entering the depth and X-position of the start and end line, in Start and End point attributes.
• You can also change the anchor for the start and end of line, by selecting from the Anchor box. Note . The X-position depends on the anchor point. You need to enter to which track the anchor is to be made, if you select either Left or Right edge of track in the Anchor section.
• To add an arrow to the line, select from the Arrow Styles .
• Click New to enter free format text that will be associated/related to the line. The Free Format Text Entry sidebar will open. Click to learn how to add free format text .
• Click OK to draw the line on the log.

Log On as GEO User Log On as GEO User
Each time the software is launched, the Log on as User dialog opens by default.
A user must log in before using the software.
Type a name for the new user, or select an existing user of that ODF from the drop box.
Click OK to start GEO.
The user name is just one item retained as part of the software's audit trail, and can be viewed in the following areas of GEO ; View Event Log View Curve Data history Enter a new User Name or Select an existing User of this ODF Type the new name in this box for a new user.
Select a name from the drop box for an existing user.
Show this dialog box each time GEO Starts The dialog box opens each time GEO Starts if the check box is selected.
For multiple users, the check box is best left selected to ensure each user correctly logs in prior to each session of GEO.
For a single user, clear the Show this dialog box every time GEO starts check box.
The dialog box will not open when a new GEO session is started.
The current user will be assumed to be the same as the last person logged-on, if no one else logs-on prior to the current GEO session.

The ribbons toolbar contains tab options that the user may select.
The toolbar is used to initiate processes in the application.
to change the scale, a user needs to select Scale on the Home tab.

Search for buttons by typing in the Tell me what you want to do.
section at the right of the ribbon.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\visualization\Navigate_GEO\Split_Screen_GEO.htm =====

Split Screen GEO Split Screen GEO To maximize the viewing potential of your logs it is possible to divide the main GEO window into two horizontal sections.
This allows you to view two totally separate areas of the plot.
This may be beneficial if you wish to compare two sections of your well log that are hundreds of feet/meters apart.
It is also possible to retain a header or trailer table data in one section whilst looking at the plot where that information refers.
To apply this feature: At the top of the main Vertical scroll bar on the right hand side of the window is a small gray bar, directly above the ‘up’ arrow.
Click and Hold with the left mouse button.
Drag down towards the middle of the screen.
The screen will now divide in two.
Two separate scroll bars will now appear, allowing you in each section to view any part of the log you wish.
To return the screen to just one whole section, simply click and hold the bar as before and drag it to the position above the top ‘up’ arrow.
You can also perform this same operation via the View tab, by selecting the Create / Close Split Window.
To split the screen so that the track legend automatically freezes on the top half of the screen, on the View tab click Freeze Legend Pane.

• At the top of the main Vertical scroll bar on the right hand side of the window is a small gray bar, directly above the ‘up’ arrow.
• Click and Hold with the left mouse button.
• Drag down towards the middle of the screen.
• Release the mouse button.
• The screen will now divide in two .

Starting a New GEO Session Starting a new GEO session GEO is launched using any of the following methods; Click the program icon ( GEO for Windows) in the Windows menu.
The GEO icon may not appear in the Start menu anymore, when you do a fresh installation of this current version of GEO.
Click the Windows button, select Geologix GEO Suite 8, then GEO.
In Windows Explorer, locate the installation location and double click the Geo.
An example of the new GEO session is shown below.
Most interactions with the program are done through the menu and its commands.
The dialog boxes that appear provide a means for entering and editing data, selecting options and executing tasks.

• Click the program icon (GEO for Windows) in the Windows menu. Note . The GEO icon may not appear in the Start menu anymore, when you do a fresh installation of this current version of GEO.
• Click the Windows button,  select Geologix GEO Suite 8 , then GEO.
• In Windows Explorer, locate the installation location and double click the Geo.exe file.

Status Bar Status Bar Currently selected printer.
The Name of the printer, followed by the printer port assigned (will be LPT1 for local printer).
The number within the brackets are the display zooms X and Y required in the Global Settings dialog bo to view the plot at printer resolution.
If an alternate depth system is defined, such as TVD, TWT or VSEC, this will be stated also.
Mouse pointer position in the the plot.
The origin (0x0) is at the screen top left.
Data range of the ODF.
Show the minimum and maximum depth of the loaded curve data.
Shows the current plot scale.
Move the slider or select the minus and plus buttons to change the zoom, or type the zoom percentage on the right.
Zoom the document so that the width of the plot matches the width of the window.
Enlarges any part of the log confined within a user defined rectangle around the section or object of interest.
If eView is disabled, this plot is not allowed to be opened by GEOe-View.
Change between enabled and disabled by right clicking on the text.

Currently selected printer. | The Name of the printer, followed by the printer port assigned (will be LPT1 for local printer). The number within the brackets are the display zooms X and Y required in the Global Settings dialog bo to view the plot at printer resolution.
Mouse pointer depth. | If an alternate depth system is defined, such as TVD, TWT or VSEC, this will be stated also.
Mouse pointer position in the the plot. | The origin (0x0) is at the screen top left.
Data range of the ODF. | Show the minimum and maximum depth of the loaded curve data.
Log scale. | Shows the current plot scale.
Zoom slider. | Move the slider or select the minus and plus buttons to change the zoom, or type the zoom percentage on the right.
Fit to screen. | Zoom the document so that the width of the plot matches the width of the window.

===== FILE: c:\Users\HaochengLin\Documents\GitHub\GEO-bot-prototype\Data\html_files\visualization\Touch_Screen_Devices\Touch_Screen_Devices.htm =====

Touch Screen Devices Touch Screen Devices
The available gestures are listed below.
Pan Use panning to see another part of a page that has scroll bars.
For example, you can pan to see part of a long document or spreadsheet that doesn't appear in the window.
Simply touch and drag the page with two fingers.
Moving objects Press and hold on the object you would like to move, drag it to it's new location and then lift your finger.
Press and hold does the same thing as right-clicking an item.
To perform the action, touch the screen where you want to right-click, hold until a complete circle appears, and then lift your finger.
The shortcut menu appears after you lift your finger.
Zoom Use zooming to make an item on the scr een larger or smaller.
Zooming in shows a smaller area in more detail; zooming out shows a larger area.
To zoom out, touch two points on the item, and then move your fingers toward each other, as if you're pinching them together.
To zoom in, touch two points on the item, and then move your fingers away from each other, as if you're stretching them apart.
